<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

Released: 14 October 2014</span></li>

<p><i><b>The Endless River</b></i> is the fifteenth and final <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a> by the British <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>. It was released by <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> in Friday-release countries on 7 November 2014, and in the United Kingdom and United States on 10 November 2014. It is Pink Floyd's first studio album since the death of keyboardist and founder member <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wright_(musician)" title="Richard Wright (musician)">Richard Wright</a>, who appears posthumously, and the third by the <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a>-led Pink Floyd following <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a>' departure in 1985. It is also the first Pink Floyd album distributed by Parlophone and <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a> following the purchase of <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> and its assets by the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a> in 2012, their transfer to Parlophone and the purchase of Parlophone by Warner Bros. in 2013.</p>
<p>Described as a "<a href="/wiki/Swan_song" title="Swan song">swan song</a>" for Wright, <i>The Endless River</i> mostly comprises <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Instrumental_music" title="Instrumental music">instrumental music</a>. It is based on 20 hours of unreleased material Pink Floyd wrote, recorded and produced with Wright during sessions for their previous studio album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Division_Bell" title="The Division Bell">The Division Bell</a></i> (1994). New material was recorded in 2013 and 2014 in Gilmour's studios the <i><a href="/wiki/Astoria_(recording_studio)" title="Astoria (recording studio)">Astoria</a></i> and Medina Studios in <a href="/wiki/Hove" title="Hove">Hove</a>, England. It was produced by Gilmour, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Glover" title="Martin Glover">Youth</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson_(recording_engineer)" title="Andrew Jackson (recording engineer)">Andy Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phil_Manzanera" title="Phil Manzanera">Phil Manzanera</a>.</p>
<p>Information about the <i>The Endless River</i> was leaked via social media, after which Pink Floyd made a formal announcement. The band, Parlophone and Columbia Records (outside Europe) launched a promotional campaign with <a href="/wiki/Television_advertisement" title="Television advertisement">television advertisements</a> and installations of the album artwork in cities around the world, including <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Album_cover" title="Album cover">cover concept</a> is by <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Emad_Eldin" title="Ahmed Emad Eldin">Ahmed Emad Eldin</a> with sleeve design by <a href="/wiki/Stylorouge" title="Stylorouge">Stylorouge</a> and creative direction by <a href="/wiki/Aubrey_Powell_(designer)" title="Aubrey Powell (designer)">Aubrey Powell</a>.</p>
<p><i>The Endless River</i> became the most pre-ordered album of all time on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_UK" title="Amazon UK">Amazon UK</a>, and debuted at number one in several countries. The vinyl edition was the fastest-selling UK vinyl release of 2014 and the fastest-selling since 1997. The album received mixed reviews.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rickwright.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="736" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Rickwright.jpg/220px-Rickwright.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Rickwright.jpg/330px-Rickwright.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Rickwright.jpg/440px-Rickwright.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rickwright.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Endless River</i> was created as a tribute to <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wright_(musician)" title="Richard Wright (musician)">Richard Wright</a>, one of the band's founding members, who died in 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the departure of founding member <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a> in 1985 and Waters' failed attempt to dissolve the band,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> guitarist and vocalist <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a> was left to lead Pink Floyd with drummer <a href="/wiki/Nick_Mason" title="Nick Mason">Nick Mason</a>. Keyboardist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wright_(musician)" title="Richard Wright (musician)">Richard Wright</a> had been fired by Waters during the recording of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall" title="The Wall">The Wall</a></i> (1979<i>),</i> but was invited back by Gilmour and Mason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obituary_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-obituary-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Under Gilmour's leadership, Pink Floyd recorded two studio albums: <i><a href="/wiki/A_Momentary_Lapse_of_Reason" title="A Momentary Lapse of Reason">A Momentary Lapse of Reason</a></i> (1987) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Division_Bell" title="The Division Bell">The Division Bell</a></i> (1994). The latter saw a greater participation from Richard Wright, who shared his first writing credits on a Pink Floyd album since <i>Wish You Were Here</i> (1975), and recorded his first lead vocal since <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Side_of_the_Moon" title="The Dark Side of the Moon">The Dark Side of the Moon</a></i> (1973).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-divisionbellliner_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-divisionbellliner-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Wright died of an undisclosed form of cancer on 15 September 2008 at the age of 65.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obituary_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-obituary-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Initial tributes to Wright included statements from Gilmour, Mason and Waters,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> tribute performances by artists such as <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> and various television and radio specials produced in the weeks following his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>The Endless River</i> has been described by the band as a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Ambient_music" title="Ambient music">ambient</a> and <a href="/wiki/Instrumental_rock" title="Instrumental rock">instrumental</a> album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NME_staff_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-NME_staff-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailymail.co.uk_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-dailymail.co.uk-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The closing track "Louder Than Words" is the album's only song to have a lead vocal track, with lyrics by David Gilmour's wife <a href="/wiki/Polly_Samson" title="Polly Samson">Polly Samson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> who also shares writing credits on Pink Floyd's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Division_Bell" title="The Division Bell">The Division Bell</a></i> and Gilmour's <i><a href="/wiki/On_an_Island" title="On an Island">On an Island</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-divisionbellliner_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-divisionbellliner-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> In a statement, Mason described the album as a tribute to Wright: "I think this record is a good way of recognising a lot of what he does and how his playing was at the heart of the Pink Floyd sound. Listening back to the sessions, it really brought home to me what a special player he was."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesquote_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimesquote-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Gilmour told <i><a href="/wiki/Mojo_(magazine)" title="Mojo (magazine)">Mojo</a></i>: "Unapologetically, this is for the generation that wants to put its headphones on, lie in a beanbag, or whatever, and get off on a piece of music for an extended period of time. You could say it’s not for the iTunes, downloading-individual-tracks generation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailymail.co.uk_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-dailymail.co.uk-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording">Recording</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recording">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:London,_The_O2,_The_Wall_Live,_2011-05-12_(19)_(6203136479).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2800" data-file-width="4976" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/London%2C_The_O2%2C_The_Wall_Live%2C_2011-05-12_%2819%29_%286203136479%29.jpg/220px-London%2C_The_O2%2C_The_Wall_Live%2C_2011-05-12_%2819%29_%286203136479%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/London%2C_The_O2%2C_The_Wall_Live%2C_2011-05-12_%2819%29_%286203136479%29.jpg/330px-London%2C_The_O2%2C_The_Wall_Live%2C_2011-05-12_%2819%29_%286203136479%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/London%2C_The_O2%2C_The_Wall_Live%2C_2011-05-12_%2819%29_%286203136479%29.jpg/440px-London%2C_The_O2%2C_The_Wall_Live%2C_2011-05-12_%2819%29_%286203136479%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:London,_The_O2,_The_Wall_Live,_2011-05-12_(19)_(6203136479).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Drummer <a href="/wiki/Nick_Mason" title="Nick Mason">Nick Mason</a> (left) and guitarist <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a> (right) took up the project in 2013, intending to create "a 21st-century Pink Floyd album".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>The Endless River</i> is based on material recorded in 1993 and 1994 during the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Division_Bell" title="The Division Bell">Division Bell</a></i> recording. The sessions were held at <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Row_Studios" title="Britannia Row Studios">Britannia Row Studios</a> and aboard the <i><a href="/wiki/Astoria_(recording_studio)" title="Astoria (recording studio)">Astoria</a></i>, where Pink Floyd's <i><a href="/wiki/A_Momentary_Lapse_of_Reason" title="A Momentary Lapse of Reason">A Momentary Lapse of Reason</a></i> (1987) and Gilmour's <i><a href="/wiki/On_an_Island" title="On an Island">On an Island</a></i> (2006) were also partly recorded. In 1994, Wright said the band had recorded "four 90-minute DATs of five or six hours of music. The hardest thing was to throw things out and decide what we're gonna work on ... but they are not lost. They are in my head, they are in Dave's head."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In the same year, Pink Floyd engineer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson_(recording_engineer)" title="Andrew Jackson (recording engineer)">Andy Jackson</a> edited the material, described by Mason as <a href="/wiki/Ambient_music" title="Ambient music">ambient music</a>, to an hour-long composition tentatively titled <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_unreleased_songs_recorded_by_Pink_Floyd#The_Big_Spliff" title="List of unreleased songs recorded by Pink Floyd">The Big Spliff</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Something_2014.2C_pp._38-45_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Something_2014.2C_pp._38-45-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Pink Floyd decided not to release it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, Gilmour and Mason decided to revisit recordings made with Wright prior to his death in 2008 to create a new Pink Floyd album. Gilmour said: "We listened to over 20 hours of the three of us playing together and selected the music we wanted to work on for the new album. Over the last year we've added new parts, re-recorded others and generally harnessed studio technology to make a 21st-century Pink Floyd album. With Rick gone, and with him the chance of ever doing it again, it feels right that these revisited and reworked tracks should be made available as part of our repertoire."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesquote_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimesquote-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Only a small part from <i>The Big Spliff</i> was used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uncut_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-uncut-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Gilmour asked guitarist and producer <a href="/wiki/Phil_Manzanera" title="Phil Manzanera">Phil Manzanera</a>, who played on and co-produced <i>On an Island</i>, to work on the material. Manzanera listened to 20 hours of recordings and, with Jackson and engineer Damon Iddins, spent six weeks assembling four 14-minute pieces. Gilmour gave the first two of these pieces to producer <a href="/wiki/Martin_Glover" title="Martin Glover">Youth</a>, who added guitar and bass parts. In November 2013, Gilmour led sessions with Manzanera, Youth and Jackson to record material with Mason, saxophonist <a href="/wiki/Gilad_Atzmon" title="Gilad Atzmon">Gilad Atzmon</a> and bassist <a href="/wiki/Guy_Pratt" title="Guy Pratt">Guy Pratt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Something_2014.2C_pp._38-45_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Something_2014.2C_pp._38-45-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Backing vocalists including <a href="/wiki/Durga_McBroom" title="Durga McBroom">Durga McBroom</a> recorded parts and Gilmour recorded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lead_vocals" title="Lead vocals">lead vocals</a> on "Louder than Words",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardfirst_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboardfirst-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> with lyrics written by Gilmour's wife <a href="/wiki/Polly_Samson" title="Polly Samson">Polly Samson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AboutER_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-AboutER-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The album comprises four pieces each taking a side of the record, with additional drum and guitar <a href="/wiki/Overdubbing" title="Overdubbing">overdubs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uncut_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-uncut-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> "Autumn '68" features a recording of Wright playing the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall_Organ" title="Royal Albert Hall Organ">Royal Albert Hall's pipe organ</a> in 1969.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woodcraft_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Woodcraft-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NMEND_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-NMEND-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The track also has additional keyboards, added more recently by Damon Iddins. Mason stated that unreleased sessions Wright recorded for Gilmour's solo projects could appear on Gilmour's future solo albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6Music_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-6Music-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Bassist and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a>, who left Pink Floyd in 1985, was not involved in the recording.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Endless River</i> is the first Pink Floyd studio album since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Dark_Side_Of_The_Moon" title="The Dark Side Of The Moon"><i>The Dark Side Of The Moon</i></a> (1973) for which <a href="/wiki/Nick_Mason" title="Nick Mason">Mason</a> is credited for writing (for Sum and Skins). Asked if <i>The Endless River</i> is the final Pink Floyd album, Gilmour replied: "Yes, I'm pretty certain that there will not be any sort of follow-up after this."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6Music_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-6Music-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Packaging">Packaging</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Packaging">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <i>Endless River</i> cover artwork depicts a man in an open shirt <a href="/wiki/Punt_(boat)" title="Punt (boat)">punting</a> across a sea of clouds towards the sun<i>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artwork-guardian_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-artwork-guardian-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The album is the fourth by Pink Floyd not to feature artwork by long-time collaborator <a href="/wiki/Storm_Thorgerson" title="Storm Thorgerson">Storm Thorgerson</a>, who died in 2013;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> with his design company <a href="/wiki/Hipgnosis" title="Hipgnosis">Hipgnosis</a>, Thorgerson designed every Pink Floyd album cover but <i><a href="/wiki/The_Piper_at_the_Gates_of_Dawn" title="The Piper at the Gates of Dawn">The Piper at the Gates of Dawn</a></i> (1967), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall" title="The Wall">The Wall</a></i> (1979) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Final_Cut_(album)" title="The Final Cut (album)">The Final Cut</a></i> (1983), including Pink Floyd's live and compilation albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Hipgnosis co-founder <a href="/wiki/Aubrey_Powell_(designer)" title="Aubrey Powell (designer)">Aubrey Powell</a> discovered 18-year-old Egyptian artist <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Emad_Eldin" title="Ahmed Emad Eldin">Ahmed Emad Eldin</a> and asked to use the concept from Eldin's piece <i>Beyond the Sky</i> for <i>The Endless River</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The final cover is a recreation of Eldin's work by London design firm <a href="/wiki/Stylorouge" title="Stylorouge">Stylorouge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artwork-egyptianstreets_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-artwork-egyptianstreets-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Eldin was a Pink Floyd fan and accepted enthusiastically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Powell felt Ahmed’s concept had "an instant Floydian resonance", and described it as "enigmatic and open to interpretation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-utsandiego_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-utsandiego-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album title is taken from a lyric on the last track and single released from <i>The Division Bell</i>, "<a href="/wiki/High_Hopes_(Pink_Floyd_song)" title="High Hopes (Pink Floyd song)">High Hopes</a>": "<i>The water flowing / The endless river / Forever and ever."</i> Gilmour said the lyric suggested "some sort of continuum" connecting the two records, since they came from the same sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6Music_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-6Music-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Deluxe.22_editions">"Deluxe" editions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title='Edit section: "Deluxe" editions'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>The Endless River</i> was also released in boxed DVD and Blu-ray "deluxe" editions, containing a 24-page hardback book, postcards, and a bonus disc of three additional music tracks and six music videos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AboutER_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-AboutER-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> These nine tracks play for a total of 39 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AboutER_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-AboutER-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The DVD edition includes the album in <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Digital" title="Dolby Digital">Dolby Digital</a> and <a href="/wiki/DTS_(sound_system)" title="DTS (sound system)">DTS</a> <a href="/wiki/5.1_surround_sound" title="5.1 surround sound">5.1 surround sound</a>, plus a 48kHz /24 bit stereo version. The Blu-ray has DTS Master Audio and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PCM" title="PCM">PCM</a>, 96/24 5.1 surround and a PCM stereo 96/24 version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AboutER_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-AboutER-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Endless_River_Installation_@_Southbank.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="333" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/The_Endless_River_Installation_%40_Southbank.jpg/220px-The_Endless_River_Installation_%40_Southbank.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/The_Endless_River_Installation_%40_Southbank.jpg/330px-The_Endless_River_Installation_%40_Southbank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/The_Endless_River_Installation_%40_Southbank.jpg/440px-The_Endless_River_Installation_%40_Southbank.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Endless_River_Installation_@_Southbank.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Several art installations, such as this one in <a href="/wiki/South_Bank" title="South Bank">South Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, were placed around the world in promotion of <i>The Endless River</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>The Endless River</i> is the second Pink Floyd album distributed by <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amazon-gb_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-amazon-gb-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> following the release of the 20th anniversary editions of <i>The Division Bell</i> earlier in 2014. <i>The Division Bell</i>, along with subsequent live and compilation albums, were previously published by <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> in Europe and <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony</a> counterpart <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> for the rest of the world.</p>
<p>Pink Floyd were affected by the <a href="/wiki/EMI#Sony.2FUniversal_sale" title="EMI">sale of EMI</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a>, which lasted from 2011 to 2013. The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> approved the sale with conditions, including the sale of certain EMI assets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Pink Floyd, along with many other bands under the <a href="/wiki/List_of_EMI_artists" title="List of EMI artists">EMI roster</a>, were transferred to different labels during the process. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Warner_Music_Group_labels#Parlophone_Label_Group" title="List of Warner Music Group labels">Parlophone Label Group</a> was formed under <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a> as one of many assets to be sold off by Universal following the acquisition of EMI, with Pink Floyd transferred to the Parlophone Label Group during the sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a>, in 2013, struck a deal with Universal to buy the Parlophone label Group from EMI, acquiring publishing rights to Pink Floyd's back catalog and future releases in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweet</a> on 5 July 2014, Pink Floyd lyricist and wife of David Gilmour, <a href="/wiki/Polly_Samson" title="Polly Samson">Polly Samson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_leak" title="Internet leak">leaked</a> information about a new Pink Floyd album, including its title and a projected release window of October 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> to pre-empt a tabloid newspaper report.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Something_2014.2C_pp._38-45_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Something_2014.2C_pp._38-45-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The announcement was followed by backing vocalist <a href="/wiki/Durga_McBroom" title="Durga McBroom">Durga McBroom</a> posting a photo of her alongside Gilmour in the recording studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Details about <i>The Endless River</i> were announced on Pink Floyd's website on 7 July, describing it as "mainly ambient" and instrumental music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Pink Floyd and Parlophone formally unveiled <i>The Endless River</i> on 22 September 2014, including the release date, artwork and track listing, accompanied by a promotional website, a <a href="/wiki/Interstitial_webpage" title="Interstitial webpage">hyperstitial</a> for the official Pink Floyd website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The site featured an <a href="/wiki/Artist%27s_statement" title="Artist's statement">artist's statement</a>, photographs from the <i>The Division Bell</i> sessions, pre-order details and two <a href="/wiki/Teaser_campaign" title="Teaser campaign">teasers</a>, one featuring a 30-second snippet of the album's second track, "It's What We Do", and a <a href="/wiki/Television_advertisement" title="Television advertisement">television advertisement</a>, featuring the album's geometric-based artwork.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pre-order" title="Pre-order">pre-orders</a> for the album on physical and digital formats started the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Prominent installations of the album's artwork were placed around the world, including a four-sided 8m tall <a href="/wiki/Billboard" title="Billboard">billboard</a> placed in <a href="/wiki/South_Bank" title="South Bank">South Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artwork-guardian_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-artwork-guardian-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-artwork-independent_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-artwork-independent-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> and large-scale poster advertisements in cities such as <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album's only song, "Louder than Words", premiered on <a href="/wiki/Chris_Evans_(presenter)" title="Chris Evans (presenter)">Chris Evans</a>' breakfast show on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">BBC Radio 2</a> as a shortened <a href="/wiki/Radio_edit" title="Radio edit">radio edit</a>. Gilmour and Mason appeared in an interview for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_6_Music" title="BBC Radio 6 Music">BBC Radio 6 Music</a> to promote the album and to discuss Wright's contributions. The track "Allons-y (1)" was made available to download from the <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> store on 4 November 2014. In the week leading up to its release, <i>The Endless River</i> broke the record for the most pre-ordered album in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_UK" title="Amazon UK">Amazon UK</a>'s history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> On 27 November the record was broken by <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/III_(Take_That_album)" title="III (Take That album)">III</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Gilmour stated that there will be no tour to support the album, saying that was "kind of impossible" without Wright.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td><i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="4/5 stars"><img alt="4/5 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" <p><i>The Endless River</i> received mixed reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_criticism" title="Music criticism">music critics</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from mainstream critics, the album has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">average</a> score of 58, which indicates "mixed or average reviews", based on 24 reviews as of 1 December 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MC_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-MC-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ludovic Hunter-Tilney of the <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> praised the album's nostalgic "Floydian" sound, reminiscent of the band's work prior to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall" title="The Wall">The Wall</a></i>, and wrote: "How fitting that a band so accustomed to loss should close their account with an engrossing elegy to their own past."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-review-financialtimes_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-review-financialtimes-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron Cooper of <a href="/wiki/The_Music" title="The Music">The Music</a> gave the album three and a half out of five, writing that the album felt "less like a swansong and more like a final homage ... the lack of vocals (save for the album’s closing track) gives the music more freedom, allowing it to speak for itself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-review-themusicau_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-review-themusicau-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Petridis" title="Alexis Petridis">Alexis Petridis</a> described it as "not a new album from an extant band, but an echo from the past – or a last, warm but slightly awkward group hug ... on those terms, it works just fine," and praised the lead single and final track "Louder than Words" as "stately, poignant and open-hearted".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-review-theguardian_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-review-theguardian-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> In <i>Rolling Stone,</i> <a href="/wiki/David_Fricke" title="David Fricke">David Fricke</a> wrote: "Wright was the steady, binding majesty in the Floyd's explorations. This album is an unexpected, welcome epitaph."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-review-rollingstone_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-review-rollingstone-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Observer</i> wrote that the album is "an understated affair but unmistakably the Floyd ... a pretty good way to call it a day."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-review-theobserver_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-review-theobserver-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>J.C. Maçek III of <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> wrote: "Without the vocals, something is very clearly missing and the listener is left wanting more. While this makes for a good album, <i>The Endless River</i> is not quite fitting to serve as the final album of the greatest rock band of their kind, to say nothing of one of the greatest rock bands of any kind ever to perform."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PM_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-PM-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Andy Gill of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> called it "just aimless jamming, one long thread of Dave Gilmour's guitar against Rick Wright's pastel keyboards and Nick Mason's tentative percussion, with nary a melody of any distinction alighted upon for the duration .... without the sparking creativity of a Syd or Roger, all that's left is ghastly faux-psychedelic dinner-party muzak."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-review-theindependent_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-review-theindependent-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>NME</i> wrote that <i>The Endless River</i> "sounds like what it is: a collection of spruced-up outtakes from 1994's <i>Division Bell</i>. On those limited terms it works well enough, and it's interesting from a certain geeky perspective, but it's never quite as satisfying or substantial as you want it to be."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-review-nme_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-review-nme-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork</a> wrote that <i>The Endless River</i> "is quintessentially and self-consciously Pink Floyd, for better or for worse ... it proves to be one of the few Pink Floyd releases that sounds like a step backwards, with nothing new to say and no new frontiers to explore."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitchfork_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Mikael Wood of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> called it "so excruciatingly dull (even by Pink Floyd's often-dull standards) that the band's name on the cover feels like a straight-up bait-and-switch."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes-review_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-review-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the week before its release, <i>The Endless River</i> displaced <i><a href="/wiki/Four_(One_Direction_album)" title="Four (One Direction album)">Four</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/One_Direction" title="One Direction">One Direction</a> as the most pre-ordered album of all time on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_UK" title="Amazon UK">Amazon UK</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnbc_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> It debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, with sales totaling 139,351 the third highest opening sales week of 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-review-theindependent_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-review-theindependent-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> making it Pink Floyd's sixth UK number one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialcharts_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-officialcharts-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialcharts2_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-officialcharts2-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 27 November 2014, the vinyl edition had sold 6,000 copies, making it the fastest-selling UK vinyl release of 2014 and the fastest-selling since 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The album also debuted at number one in several other countries, including France, Germany, Portugal, Ireland, the Netherlands, Belgium, New Zealand,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialcharts_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-officialcharts-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> and Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ajournalofmusicalthings_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-ajournalofmusicalthings-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> In the US, it debuted at number 3 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with 170,000 copies sold in its first week;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> as of January 2015, it has sold 355,000 copies there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Track_listing">Track listing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Track listing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel.5B72.5D">Personnel<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Endless_River&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personnel[72]">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>Pink Floyd</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a> – <a href="/wiki/Guitar" title="Guitar">guitars</a> (all but 3), EBow guitar (1, 3, 10), <a href="/wiki/Singing" title="Singing">lead vocals</a> (18), backing vocals (7, 15, 17), <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_instrument" title="Keyboard instrument">keyboards</a> (7, 15, 16), <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> (6, 7), <a href="/wiki/EMS_VCS_3" title="EMS VCS 3">EMS VCS 3</a> (4, 6), <a href="/wiki/Bass_guitar" title="Bass guitar">bass guitar</a> (2, 4, 7, 17), Hammond organ (18), percussion (8), <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(music)" title="Sampling (music)">voice samples</a> (1)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nick_Mason" title="Nick Mason">Nick Mason</a> – <a href="/wiki/Drum_kit" title="Drum kit">drums</a> (2, 4, 5, 7, 9, 11, 13, 14, 16, 17, 18) <a href="/wiki/Percussion_instrument" title="Percussion instrument">percussion</a> (15, 18), rototoms (5), gong (5, 12, 16), voice samples (1)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Wright_(musician)" title="Richard Wright (musician)">Richard Wright</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hammond_organ" title="Hammond organ">Hammond organ</a> (1, 11, 13, 16), <a href="/wiki/Farfisa" title="Farfisa">Farfisa organ</a> (4, 6, 14, 16), <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall_Organ" title="Royal Albert Hall Organ">pipe organ</a> (12), <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> (4, 6, 8, 14, 18), <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_piano" title="Rhodes piano">Rhodes piano</a> (9, 18), electric piano (3), <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_instrument" title="Keyboard instrument">keyboards</a> (1, 2, 5, 16, 17), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synthesiser" title="Synthesiser">synthesiser</a> (1, 2, 8, 10, 14, 17, 18), voice samples (1)</li>
</ul>

<dt>Additional musicians</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guy_Pratt" title="Guy Pratt">Guy Pratt</a> – bass guitar (9, 14)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Ezrin" title="Bob Ezrin">Bob Ezrin</a> – bass guitar (11, 13, 18), additional keyboards (1)</li>

<li>Damon Iddins – additional keyboards (4, 12)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anthony_Moore" title="Anthony Moore">Anthony Moore</a> – keyboards (15)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gilad_Atzmon" title="Gilad Atzmon">Gilad Atzmon</a> – <a href="/wiki/Tenor_saxophone" title="Tenor saxophone">tenor saxophone</a> (7), <a href="/wiki/Clarinet" title="Clarinet">clarinet</a> (7)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Escala_(group)" title="Escala (group)">Escala</a>:
<ul>
<li>Chantal Leverton – <a href="/wiki/Viola" title="Viola">viola</a> (18)</li>
